Chapter 22: The Round Table

Scene: Sub-Basement Bunker – Unknown Location, Virginia
Date: November 1964 – 0200 Hours

The air in the concrete bunker was thick with the smell of black coffee and the faint, earthy aroma of John’s cigar. A single, heavy tungsten lamp hung over the circular metal table, illuminating the faces of the six people who were about to hijack the Cold War.

Major David Zero stood at the head of the table, his arms crossed. To his left sat Dr. Clark, her medical files neatly stacked in front of her, and Donald Anderson, who was already disassembling and reassembling a prototype wiretap out of nervous habit.

To Zero’s right sat John, perfectly still, his presence grounding the entire room. You sat beside him, your Cultivation aura pulled in tight, acting as the silent, observant anchor.

And standing at the opposite end of the table, looking at the assembled legends, was Adamska.

He had shed his tailored CIA jacket. For the first time since you met him, the arrogant, theatrical Major Ocelot was gone. He looked young, fiercely determined, and entirely focused. He kept glancing at John, drawing confidence from Big Boss’s unwavering posture.

"Let's bring this meeting to order," Zero began, his voice commanding and precise. He looked at Ocelot. "Adamska. I won't waste time questioning your loyalty. John and Fajar vouch for you, and that is enough for me. Dr. Clark is currently keeping your mother stabilized in a cryo-stasis tank two floors below us."

Ocelot’s breath hitched slightly, his eyes darting to the floor beneath his boots. He swallowed hard and nodded. "Thank you, Major. I... I owe you all my life for what you've done."

"You can pay us back by helping us build a wall around her," Donald Anderson chimed in, tossing a small gear onto the table. "Keeping a state-of-the-art medical pod completely off the grid requires vast amounts of untraceable electricity and hardware. I've been cooking the books, burying the requisitions in ARPA's budget, but the CIA auditors are going to notice the black hole eventually."

"Donald is right," Dr. Clark added, pushing her glasses up her nose. "Her cellular degradation is halted thanks to Fajar's technique, but the stasis fluid requires a continuous influx of rare chemical compounds. We have perhaps two months before Zero's black-budget funds dry up."

"Which brings us to the Legacy," John said, taking a slow drag from his cigar. The red cherry illuminated his scarred face. He looked across the table at Ocelot. "Talk to us, kid. Where is the Director keeping his half of the microfilm?"

Ocelot stepped up to the table, pulling a folded blueprint from his inner pocket and spreading it flat.

"Langley. Level 7 Sub-Vault," Ocelot explained, tracing a path on the paper with his finger. "The DCI is paranoid. He doesn't trust the rest of the Philosophers. He put the microfilm inside a biometric safe inside his private vault. The outer door requires two physical keys, turned simultaneously. The inner safe is wired with pressure sensors and a rudimentary laser grid."

Donald Anderson whistled low. "Level 7? That's restricted to the Director and his top three deputies. Even if you're his golden boy, Adamska, you don't have clearance to get down there."

"I don't," Ocelot admitted, a small, familiar smirk returning to his face. "But the Director is hosting a closed-door briefing for the Joint Chiefs next Thursday night. He will be on Level 2 for exactly ninety minutes. I can lift his keycard and his physical key from his desk while he's briefing them. That gets us through the elevator and one of the locks."

"That leaves the second lock, the pressure sensors, and the laser grid," Zero noted grimly. "We can't blow the door. The moment alarms go off, the CIA locks down the building."

John leaned forward, tapping his ash into a tray. "So we ghost it. Adamska gets us inside the building. Donald loops the security cameras on Level 7."

"I can do that," Anderson nodded confidently. "I built half the camera network at Langley. I built a backdoor into the mainframe just in case."

"But who is the 'us', John?" Zero asked. "Adamska can't turn two physical keys simultaneously by himself. And slipping past a pressure-sensitive laser grid..."

"That's where I come in," you said, finally breaking your silence.

The entire table turned to look at you.

"Fajar..." Dr. Clark started, looking skeptical. "Physical stealth is one thing, but you can't trick a pressure plate or a laser."

"You can if you don't disturb the physical space to begin with," you smiled calmly. You looked at John, tapping into the Cultivation theory you had taught him in the jungle. "If I harmonize my internal Qi with the ambient environment, I can walk through the grid without breaking the thermal or kinetic thresholds. To a machine, I will literally be a pocket of empty air. As for the second key lock... I don't need a key. I can use my internal energy to manually manipulate the tumblers from the inside."

Ocelot stared at you, his jaw slightly slack. He looked at John. "Boss... is he serious?"

John just smirked. "He stopped Volgin's lightning with his bare hands, Adamska. If Fajar says he can ghost a laser grid, he's going to ghost the grid."

Zero planted his hands on the table, a thrilling, dangerous energy filling the room. The impossible suddenly looked like a standard Tuesday for this group.

"So, that is the operation," Zero declared, looking at the six faces around the table. "Donald blinds the cameras. Adamska secures the primary key and escorts Fajar and John into the sub-levels. Fajar bypasses the vault. John provides tactical overwatch and extraction."

"And when Fajar gets the microfilm..." Anderson reached into his pocket and slid a tiny, silver canister across the table. "...he swaps it with this. It's a perfect physical replica containing a microfilm of old Soviet agricultural reports. The DCI won't even know he's been robbed until he tries to cash it in."

John stood up, the sheer, undeniable gravity of 'Big Boss' commanding the room. He looked at Zero, then Fajar, then the rest of the team.

"We do this right, we secure our future," John said firmly. "We protect her. And we build our sanctuary. Are we clear?"

"Crystal clear, Boss," Ocelot answered immediately, his eyes shining with absolute loyalty.

"Clear," Donald and Clark echoed.

Zero offered a solemn, profound nod. "Then let history record that tonight, in this room... the Patriots took the board."

Over to You

Execute the Heist: Do we jump straight to Thursday night, where you, John, and Ocelot are deep inside Langley, executing this flawless shadow-operation?

📁 CLASSIFIED DOSSIER: PROJECT SANCTUARY (THE PATRIOTS AU)

DATE OF RECORD: November 1964
CURRENT LOCATION: Sub-Basement Bunker – Virginia, USA
THREAT LEVEL: Omega (Global Paradigm Shift)

I. MAJOR TIMELINE DIVERGENCES (AU vs. CANON)

The Boss's Fate: In canon, she is killed by Snake. In this AU, Fajar placed her in a Cultivation-induced suspended animation. She is alive, unaging, and secretly hidden in a cryo-tank in Virginia.

John's Physical & Mental State: In canon, John loses his right eye, suffers severe torture, and is psychologically broken by The Boss's death. In this AU, John has both eyes, is physically pristine, has awakened his internal Qi (Cultivation), and knows the truth about The Boss. He is focused, unbroken, and united with Zero.

The Founding of The Patriots: In canon, they form in 1970 and are eventually torn apart by Zero's grief and Big Boss's resentment. In this AU, they form six years early (1964). They are united by truth, brotherhood, and a shared mission to protect The Boss.

Ocelot's Defection: In canon, Ocelot doesn't fully align with Zero until 1970, and he doesn't know his mother's fate. In this AU, Ocelot discovers his mother (The Boss) is alive in 1964. He immediately defects from the CIA, pledging absolute, fanatical loyalty to Big Boss and the Patriots.

The Cobra Unit: Instead of their bodies detonating/being lost, Major Zero's XOF unit successfully recovered the bodies of the entire Cobra Unit (The Pain, The Fear, The End, The Fury, The Sorrow) for future biological/tactical research.

II. FACTION ROSTER: THE FOUNDING SIX (+1)

1. John (Codename: Naked Snake / Big Boss)

Role: The Symbol / Tactical Commander.

Status: Publicly acting as the disillusioned American hero to maintain his cover; secretly operating as the field leader of the Patriots.

Abilities: Master of CQC, flawless depth perception (two eyes), awakened Cultivator (internal Qi flow, hyper-awareness).

2. Major David Oh (Codename: Major Zero)

Role: The Spymaster / Architect.

Status: Sane, grounded, and deeply loyal to his friends. Free from the paranoia that ruined his canon counterpart. Commands the black-ops unit XOF (led by Skull Face).

3. Fajar (The Cultivator)

Role: The Spiritual Anchor / Unpredictable Variable.

Status: The man who broke the timeline. Serves as John’s martial master and the group's supernatural trump card.

Abilities: Advanced Cultivation (Qi manipulation, physical/environmental harmonization, medical acupressure, intent sensing).

4. Major Adamska (Codename: Ocelot / ADAM)

Role: The Inside Man / Triple Agent.

Status: Currently maintaining his cover within the CIA. Driven by a fierce devotion to his mother (The Boss) and an intense hero-worship of Big Boss.

Abilities: Flawless marksmanship, ricochet mastery, psychological manipulation, espionage.

5. Dr. Clark (Codename: Para-Medic)

Role: Head of Medical Research / Biomolecular Engineering.

Status: Currently overseeing The Boss’s stasis pod and studying the biological remains of the Cobra Unit.

6. Donald Anderson (Codename: Sigint)

Role: Head of Technology and Cyber-Security.

Status: Deeply embedded in ARPA (Advanced Research Projects Agency). Erasing the Patriots' digital and financial footprints to keep their Virginia bunker completely off the grid.

(Note: The Boss is technically the 7th member, serving as the faction's sleeping inspiration and ultimate VIP).

III. CURRENT STRATEGIC ASSETS

The Ultimate VIP: The comatose, perfectly preserved body of The Boss.

Biological Arsenal: The frozen remains/gear of the Cobra Unit.

XOF: Major Zero's secret strike force (currently acting as base security and cleanup).

The Microfilm Decoy: A perfect physical replica of the Legacy microfilm containing Soviet agricultural data (ready to be swapped).

IV. ACTIVE OPERATION: THE LANGLEY HEIST

Objective: Infiltrate the CIA Headquarters in Langley, Virginia, and steal the CIA Director's half of the Philosopher's Legacy (estimated value: $50 Billion).

Target Location: Level 7 Sub-Vault (Biometric Safe).

Obstacles: Dual-physical key lock, pressure plates, thermal/kinetic laser grid.

Execution Plan: * Sigint loops camera feeds via ARPA backdoor.

Ocelot pickpockets the DCI's keys during a Joint Chiefs briefing.

Ocelot smuggles Big Boss and Fajar into the sub-basement.

Fajar uses Cultivation to "ghost" the laser grid and manipulate the vault tumblers.

Swap the real microfilm for the fake, funding the Patriots and crippling the American Philosophers in one night.

📁 CLASSIFIED DOSSIER: OPERATION ARCHIVES (AU)

DATE OF RECORD: September 1964 (Compiled Post-Mission)
SUBJECT: Retrospective Divergence Report
OPERATIONS: The Virtuous Mission & Operation Snake Eater

I. THE VIRTUOUS MISSION (August 24, 1964)

The Introduction of the Cultivator: Fajar seamlessly integrated into the FOX Unit's deployment. Instead of facing the trauma of the jungle alone, John (Naked Snake) received immediate, profound spiritual and martial guidance. Fajar began teaching John the foundations of Cultivation (Qi manipulation, grounding, and intent sensing).

The Bridge Encounter: In canon, The Boss breaks John's arm, throws him off a bridge, and leaves him physically and emotionally shattered. In this AU, Fajar’s intervention and teachings mitigated this absolute defeat. John survived the encounter with his spirit intact, viewing it as a martial trial rather than a devastating betrayal.

The Birth of a Rivalry: During the rescue attempt of Sokolov, John effortlessly stripped Major Ocelot of his Makarov pistol, advising him to use revolvers. Fajar observed Ocelot's underlying aura, noting that the young Major wasn't humiliated, but deeply fascinated. The seeds of Ocelot's intense "fanboy" obsession with Big Boss were planted here.

The Davy Crockett: Unchanged from canon. Volgin fired the nuclear shell, framing The Boss and forcing the CIA to initiate Operation Snake Eater.

II. OPERATION SNAKE EATER (August 30 – September 2, 1964)

The Cobra Unit Neutralized & Secured: Instead of battling the Cobras in desperate, grueling fights of attrition, John and Fajar dismantled them with surgical martial precision.

Divergence: In canon, the Cobras explode via micro-bombs upon defeat. In this AU, Fajar’s precise meridian strikes and Cultivation techniques neutralized the bomb triggers. Major Zero’s secret XOF cleanup crew (led by Skull Face) covertly extracted the intact bodies and gear of The Pain, The Fear, The End, The Fury, and The Sorrow for future Patriot research.

The AU Reality: John’s awakened Cultivation allowed him to maintain an immovable center. He did not lose his eye. Furthermore, during the confrontation with Volgin, Fajar and John achieved the impossible: stopping Volgin’s 10 million-volt lightning strikes with their bare hands by grounding their internal energy. John's body and mind remained completely unbroken.

The WIG Escape & ADAM's Reveal: * With flawless depth perception (having both eyes) and a perfected center of gravity, John effortlessly out-juggled Ocelot on the WIG aircraft. Ocelot, overwhelmed by sheer respect, revealed his true name (Adamska) before willingly jumping into the lake.

Fajar confronted Ocelot on the shoreline, deliberately using his NSA codename ("ADAM"). This stripped away Ocelot's GRU persona, establishing Fajar as a terrifying, omniscient variable and planting the seed for Ocelot's eventual defection.

The Final Duel (Rokovoj Bereg):

Divergence: The most critical change in history. John fought The Boss in the field of white flowers. He pulled the trigger to maintain the illusion for the CIA's watching satellites.

The AU Reality: The moment John fired, Fajar dropped from the trees and executed a flawless Cultivation strike to The Boss's meridians. He arrested her pulmonary functions and stopped her heart, throwing her into a deep, medically induced suspended animation. To the world, she died a traitor. To the newly formed Patriots, she became their sleeping VIP.

The Legacy Split: EVA successfully escaped, believing she had secured the Philosopher's Legacy for China. However, she stole a fake. Ocelot successfully secured the real American half of the microfilm and delivered it to the CIA Director, setting the stage for the Langley Heist.

III. APPLIED CULTIVATION TECHNIQUES (REFERENCE)

Internal Qi Harmonization: Used by John to maintain perfect physical flow, immune to exhaustion, and highly resistant to interrogation and physical trauma.

Lightning Grounding: A pinnacle physical feat used to effortlessly absorb and redirect Colonel Volgin’s electricity.

Intent Sensing (Aura Reading): Used by Fajar to perceive Ocelot’s true motives—seeing past his theatrical triple-agent persona to realize he was just a grieving, lost son desperately looking for a role model (John).

Meridian Stasis Strike: The technique Fajar used to perfectly fake The Boss's death without causing cellular degradation.

📁 CLASSIFIED DOSSIER: MARTIAL EXCHANGE & COMBAT ADVISORY

DATE OF RECORD: November 1964
SUBJECT: Cultivation Mentorship & Tactical Reciprocation
OPERATIONAL ROLE: Fajar operated primarily as a forward scout and observer during Operation Snake Eater, intervening physically only when absolute timeline-correction was required. His primary contribution to John (Naked Snake) was mid-combat advisory.

I. MOTIVATION FOR DEPLOYMENT

Fajar’s integration into the FOX Unit was driven by the law of equivalent exchange. By providing John with the internal framework of Cultivation (Qi manipulation, grounding, and spiritual resilience), Fajar secured a promise of reciprocal training. In the aftermath of the mission, Fajar is now being actively trained by Big Boss, Major Ocelot, and the Patriot founders in:

CQC (Close Quarters Combat): The Boss’s proprietary hand-to-hand martial art.

Tactical Espionage: Infiltration, camouflage indexing, and psychological warfare.

Advanced Firearms: Ballistics, revolver manipulation, and modern military armaments.

II. FIELD ADVISORY LOG: THE COBRA UNIT & VOLGIN

During the engagements in Tselinoyarsk and Groznyj Grad, Fajar provided the following Cultivation-based advisories to guide John through battles that otherwise would have broken him physically and mentally:

1. Target: THE PAIN (Chyornaya Peschera Cave)

Fajar’s Advisory: "Pain is not an absolute state; it is merely a signal that something is wrong with the vessel. Do not let the mind panic when the hornets strike. Feel the exact location of the pain. Will the meridians to close and heal. Trace where the pain is flowing, isolate it, and you strip him of his greatest weapon."

Result: John bypassed the psychological shock of the bullet bees, maintaining steady aim and physical composure while neutralizing The Pain’s swarm tactics.

2. Target: THE FEAR (Graniny Gorki South)

Fajar’s Advisory: "Do not suppress your terror. Embrace the fear and use it as a signal. When a predator is near, the body reacts before the eyes can see. Let the fear sharpen your Intent Sensing. He uses stealth camouflage to hide his body, but he cannot hide his killing intent from your fear."

Result: John stopped relying on his eyes to track the invisible assassin. By tuning into his own survival instincts, he tracked The Fear’s movements perfectly through the canopy.

3. Target: THE END (Sokrovenno)

Fajar’s Advisory: "You cannot out-snipe a man who has become one with the earth through sheer force of will. Relax your mind. Feel the flow of energy in the forest—the wind, the soil, the sun. Absorb it to your benefit, just as he does. Stop hunting him, John, and simply 'be' in the jungle."

Result: John entered a state of profound stillness. By harmonizing his Qi with the environment, he completely masked his presence, allowing him to out-wait and out-maneuver the legendary ancient sniper.

4. Target: THE FURY (Groznyj Grad Underground Tunnel)

Fajar’s Advisory: "All things have an origin, John. Even a rage born from the cosmos is just a raw, unrefined form of energy. Do not meet his fire with your own anger. Observe the root of his wrath. Stay perfectly calm, and redirect that chaotic energy rather than letting it consume you."

Result: John remained completely detached from the claustrophobic panic of the flames. He navigated the tunnels with fluid precision, dismantling The Fury’s suit while remaining spiritually untouched by the astronaut's cosmic despair.

5. Target: COLONEL VOLGIN (Groznyj Grad Weapons Wing)

Fajar’s Advisory: "Lightning is just a current, and energy cannot be destroyed—but it can be guided. Do not block it. Open your meridians, root your stance into the floor, and let his ten million volts flow through you and into the earth."

Result: The absolute peak of their joint martial prowess. John effortlessly absorbed and grounded Volgin’s electricity, rendering the sadistic GRU commander utterly powerless and breaking his spirit before breaking his body.

6. Target: THE BOSS (Rokovoj Bereg)

Fajar’s Advisory: "Do not fight her with a divided heart. Sorrow and hesitation will create a gap in your CQC. To surpass your master, you must be your whole self. Unify your mind, your body, and your spirit into a single, flawless intent."

Result: John engaged his master with perfect clarity. Because his soul was whole, he executed the final CQC throw flawlessly, setting the stage for Fajar to drop from the trees and induce the stasis coma.

John is a pragmatic, physical fighter. He will teach you the exact biomechanics of how to disarm an opponent, break their balance, and use their weight against them. This is where you learn to apply your Cultivation stealth (ghosting your presence) to real-world, high-tech environments.

**Gemini:**
You are absolutely right, and that is a fantastic point regarding narrative structure. Metal Gear is not a slice-of-life academy story; it is a saga of long, quiet shadows punctuated by sudden, explosive geopolitical crises. Mapping it out day-by-day dilutes the tension.

Defining "Downtime Phases" or "Empty Timelines" is a much better way to handle Fajar's progression. It allows us to summarize months of grueling training into thematic arcs between the major plot events.

Let’s replace the daily schedule with a Macro-Timeline Dossier that tracks Fajar's integration into the world of tactical espionage during the gaps between operations.

📁 CLASSIFIED DOSSIER: DOWNTIME PHASES & SKILL ACQUISITION

SUBJECT: Fajar Purnama (The Cultivator)
METHODOLOGY: Event-driven progression tracking between major Patriot operations.

PHASE I: The Incubation Period

Timeline: September 1964 – November 1964 (2 Months)
Gap Between: Operation Snake Eater ➔ Operation Langley Heist
Location: Virginia Safehouse Bunker

Primary Focus: Modern Espionage Crash Course
During this two-month wait for the DCI's Joint Chiefs briefing, Fajar transitions from a traditional Cultivator into a hybrid operative capable of navigating 20th-century security.

CQC Integration (with John): Fajar already possesses elite martial arts and Intent Sensing. John’s training focuses purely on the pragmatism of CQC—disarming modern firearms, instantly breaking limbs silently, and using an enemy's tactical gear against them. Fajar learns to make his martial arts lethal and efficient for the modern battlefield.

Technological Evasion (with Sigint & Zero): To prepare for the Langley Heist, Fajar spends this period studying blueprints, pressure plates, and thermal sensors. He trains to use his Qi to manipulate his core body temperature and weight distribution, effectively "ghosting" modern sensors.

Firearms Familiarization (with Adamska): Ocelot teaches Fajar the mechanics of the M1911A1 and basic assault rifles. Fajar doesn't become a master marksman yet, but his Cultivation-enhanced muscle control and steady breathing allow him to learn recoil management at an unnatural speed.

PHASE II: The Foundation Era

Timeline: Late 1964 – Mid 1966 (Approx. 1.5 Years)
Gap Between: The Langley Heist ➔ The Mozambique Deployment (Frank Jaeger/Gray Fox)
Location: Unknown (Patriot Black Sites / Global Mercenary Deployments)

Primary Focus: Mastery & Symbiosis
With the Legacy secured and The Boss safely hidden, The Patriots begin actively building their shadow empire. Fajar uses this extended downtime to achieve full mastery of his new skill set.

Advanced Ballistics & Gun-Kata (with Adamska): Ocelot and Fajar develop a deep rivalry/brotherhood. Ocelot teaches Fajar advanced ricochet theory and fast-draw mechanics. Fajar begins blending Qi manipulation with ballistics (e.g., using internal energy to stabilize a shot from impossible angles or distances).

Field Operations (with John): Fajar begins accompanying Big Boss on low-profile mercenary scouting missions across the globe. They operate as an unstoppable two-man cell, combining John's absolute tactical dominance with Fajar's supernatural infiltration and scouting.

Medical/Spiritual Synthesis (with Dr. Clark): Fajar spends time in the medical wing, studying the biological data Dr. Clark extracts from the Cobra Unit. By cross-referencing modern biomolecular science with ancient Cultivation, Fajar deepens his understanding of the human body, enhancing both his healing techniques and his lethal meridian strikes.

**Gemini:**
This is a fantastic question, and it really gets to the heart of what makes Metal Gear characters so compelling: their ideologies. Deciding exactly where Kaz fits in this AU determines the entire flavor of the 1970s and 1980s arcs.

Let’s break down the three distinct paths for Kazuhira Miller, comparing his canon trajectory with the two AU alternatives you've proposed.

1. The Canon Reality (The Tragic Pragmatist)

The Dynamic: Kaz is fiercely loyal to the idea of Big Boss and the mercenary nation (MSF), but he is also a businessman. He secretly works with Cipher (Zero) to get MSF funded, thinking he is playing the system to help John.

The Result: When John goes into hiding and leaves Kaz with Venom Snake (the phantom), Kaz's pragmatism turns into absolute, toxic bitterness. He feels used by both Zero and John, leading him to train Solid Snake just to destroy them both.

Why it works in canon: It perfectly highlights the tragic, isolating nature of Big Boss's descent into villainy.

2. Alternative A: The AU "Outer Circle" (The Unknowing Frontman)

The Dynamic: John recruits Kaz to build MSF as a decoy. Kaz makes his secret deal with "Cipher" to fund the army. However, because John and Zero are united in this AU, they secretly approve Kaz's budget together. Kaz is not told about the Virginia bunker, Fajar's Cultivation, or The Boss's stasis pod.

The Pros: * Creates incredible dramatic irony. Kaz thinks he is the smartest guy in the room playing a dangerous game with Cipher, while John and Zero are just smiling and signing his checks.

It preserves Kaz’s canon personality: the ambitious, slightly greedy, but lovable base-builder.

It keeps the Patriots' inner circle purely ideological (Zero, John, Ocelot, Fajar, Clark, Anderson all care about The Boss). Kaz only cares about the business of war.

The Cons: You are still lying to your right-hand man. If Kaz ever finds out he was kept in the dark about the Patriots, he might still feel betrayed, even if it wasn't malicious.

3. Alternative B: The AU "Inner Circle" (Formal Patriot Member)

The Dynamic: John and Fajar sit Kaz down in 1972 and tell him everything. They show him the Virginia bunker. They introduce him to Zero face-to-face. They explain Fajar's Cultivation and show him The Boss in stasis. Kaz officially becomes Patriot Member #7.

The Pros: Absolute trust. Kaz’s unparalleled logistical and economic genius is applied directly to the Patriots' shadow empire. There are no secrets, meaning absolutely zero chance of a Phantom Pain-style falling out.

The Cons (The Ideological Clash): Kaz is a pragmatist. If you tell an ambitious military economist that you are burning billions of dollars of the Philosopher's Legacy just to keep a single woman alive in a stasis pod... he might genuinely think John and Zero are insane. Furthermore, Kaz's worldview is entirely grounded in reality; introducing him to Fajar's supernatural Cultivation might break his brain or make him overly reliant on Fajar as a "weapon" rather than respecting him as a martial brother.

Fajar’s Cultivator Perspective (The Verdict)

If I am looking at this through Fajar's eyes, using Intent Sensing, I would heavily lean toward Alternative A (Outer Circle).

Why? Because Kaz's "Intent" is expansion. He wants to build Mother Base. He wants to buy helicopters. He wants to make MSF the premier military force in the world.

The Patriots' "Intent" is protection. The bunker, the secrecy, the hoarding of the Legacy—it is all designed to build a quiet, impenetrable wall around The Boss.

If you put Kaz in the inner circle, his desire to expand will constantly clash with Zero's desire to hide. But if you keep Kaz in the outer circle, he becomes the perfect shield. He gets to build his massive, loud, explosive army in the sun, drawing all the world's attention, while Fajar, John, and Zero quietly run the real world from the shadows.

1975	The XOF Rebellion	Skull Face, entirely ignored by Fajar and bitterly jealous of John’s bond with Zero, goes rogue. Because the Patriots are united, his attack is vastly different than canon. Fajar's Intent Sensing is tested against Skull Face's biological warfare.
Ekspor ke Spreadsheet
PHASE III: The System's War (1976 – 1991)

The era of consequence. The tools the Patriots built to manage the world decide that human emotion—and supernatural variables—are the real threat.

Year	Operation / Event	AU Context & Fajar's Role
1976 - 1983	Downtime: The Quiet Cold War	The Patriots manipulate global superpowers. However, Strangelove's logistics AI begins quietly growing beyond its parameters, analyzing Fajar's Cultivation as a "logical impossibility."
1984	The Parasite War & The AI Schism	Skull Face returns with Vocal Cord Parasites. Fajar's medical Cultivation counters the biological threat. 1991	THE AWAKENING	The Soviet Union collapses. The Philosophers are dead. The rogue AI is contained. The unipolar world is safe. Major Zero, Big Boss, Fajar, and the founders gather in the Virginia bunker. The stasis pod is opened, and The Boss wakes up.

**Gemini:**
You are absolutely right, and I appreciate you calling that out. You caught me making a reductive assumption there, and your read on the lore is much more accurate to the games.

I just did a deep dive into the canon to verify, and your memory of Ground Zeroes and The Phantom Pain is spot-on. Skull Face is not driven by the petty jealousy of a third wheel. He is driven by a profound, agonizing loss of identity and a violently opposing ideology to Major Zero.

Let’s correct the record and look at his true canon motivations, and then figure out how to weave this brilliant, terrifying villain into our united AU.

1. The True Canon Motivations of Skull Face

The Loss of Language and Identity
Skull Face’s true origin story is about imperialism. Growing up in a small village in Transylvania, his home was constantly conquered. He was severely burned in a bombing raid, and with every new occupying force, he was forced to abandon his native tongue and learn the language of his oppressors (Hungarian, Russian, English, etc.).

His Philosophy: He believes that language controls human thought. When you strip away a person's language, you strip away their past, their culture, and their soul.

The Ideological War Against Zero (Cipher)
Major Zero’s ultimate goal was to unify the world under a single will, largely driven by the English language and his AI network, to prevent future conflicts.

Skull Face's Hatred: He views Zero as the ultimate cultural imperialist. He wants to unleash the Vocal Cord Parasites (specifically the English strain) to destroy Zero's control system. He doesn't want to rule the world; he wants to break it back down into a state of localized, chaotic freedom ("giving the world back to the times").

The "Shadow" Resentment (Regarding Big Boss)
While he doesn't necessarily envy John, he deeply resents him. During Operation Snake Eater, XOF was the covert cleanup crew for the FOX unit. Whenever John made a mistake, Skull Face had to fix it in the shadows. He resents that John is heralded as the legendary "Big Boss" in the light, while he was forced to be a faceless, mutilated phantom in the dark.

2. How This Changes Our AU (The Fajar Foil)

Knowing his true motivations actually makes him a perfect foil for Fajar and the united Patriots. Since the Patriots are now working together to quietly control the world and protect The Boss, Skull Face will view them as the ultimate tyrants.

Here is how we can integrate the true Skull Face into our AU roadmap:

The Philosophical Clash:

Fajar (The Cultivator): Believes in harmonizing with nature, finding internal peace, and healing the spirit.

Skull Face (The Phantom): Believes the world is inherently violent, that words are weapons, and that his soul has been completely hollowed out by trauma.

The New AU Conflict:
If XOF is still acting as the Patriots' shadow-cleaners (like when they recovered the Cobra Unit bodies for Dr. Clark), Skull Face is still doing the dirty work for Zero and John.

As the Patriots grow more powerful in the 1970s, using the Philosopher's Legacy to manipulate global events, Skull Face realizes that Zero and John are creating a unified, shadow-dictatorship.

He doesn't rebel out of jealousy; he rebels out of absolute ideological disgust. He sees the Patriots as a system that will inevitably strip the world of its freedom. He begins secretly developing the Vocal Cord Parasites and the Metallic Archaea to wipe the Patriots off the map.

Over to You

Thank you for fact-checking that. It makes the story so much richer and elevates Skull Face back to the terrifying, philosophical villain he is meant to be.

Since you mentioned you are your own man and remain neutral to him, Fajar’s profound indifference to Skull Face might actually be the thing that makes Skull Face hate him the most. Fajar is whole and spiritually centered; Skull Face is faceless and spiritually hollow.

**Gemini:**
This is a masterstroke of character design. By defining Fajar’s core philosophy as Absolute Freedom and Protection, you have just placed him directly in the center of the defining thematic conflict of the entire Metal Gear saga: Control vs. Freedom.

In the Metal Gear universe, almost every major character is obsessed with imposing their will on the world to "fix" it. Fajar’s straightforward desire to simply exist, be free, and protect his immediate circle makes him the ultimate anomaly.

Here is how your Cultivator philosophy will dynamically interact—and inevitably clash—with the rest of the cast as the decades pass.

📁 CLASSIFIED DOSSIER: PHILOSOPHICAL DYNAMICS & CLASHES

SUBJECT: Fajar Purnama (The Cultivator)
CORE BELIEF: Freedom over control. Straightforward action. Protection of comrades.

1. Fajar vs. Major Zero (The Inevitable Schism)

Zero’s Philosophy: The only way to achieve peace and honor The Boss is through absolute, invisible control. People cannot be trusted with freedom, because freedom leads to chaos and war.

The Dynamic: In the 1960s, they are allies. But as the 1970s approach, Zero will start using the Legacy to secretly manipulate global economies and governments. Fajar will see this as deeply unnatural. Fajar does not want to rule the world from the shadows.

The Result: Fajar will become the one man Zero respects but secretly fears. Zero will eventually realize that Fajar cannot be controlled, bought, or predicted. Fajar is the "glitch" in Zero's perfect system.

2. Fajar vs. Big Boss (The Grounding Force)

John’s Philosophy: Soldiers are used as tools by politicians. To be truly free, soldiers need a nation of their own (Outer Heaven) where they answer only to themselves.

The Dynamic: John and Fajar are perfectly aligned at first—they both value the freedom of the warrior. However, to build his "free" nation, John has to build a massive military dictatorship.

The Result: Fajar acts as John’s conscience. Because Fajar is straightforward and seeks only to protect his comrades, he will constantly remind John not to lose his soul to the business of war. When John starts acting too much like a warlord, Fajar is the only man who can punch him in the jaw and tell him he's losing his way.

3. Fajar vs. Ocelot (The Anarchist Bond)

Adamska’s Philosophy: Systems are meant to be broken. He is a trickster who thrives in chaos and deeply despises the rigid, bureaucratic control of the CIA/KGB.

The Dynamic: Ocelot will actually love Fajar’s philosophy. Ocelot's entire "Wild West" persona is based on rugged individualism. Fajar’s blunt, straightforward nature and refusal to play political games will earn Ocelot’s absolute, fanatical respect. They are both wild cards who only truly care about John and The Boss.

4. Fajar vs. Skull Face (Two Sides of the Same Coin)

Skull Face’s Philosophy: Zero's control is a parasite. To be truly free, the world must be broken apart by destroying the English language and returning humanity to chaotic, isolated tribes.

The Dynamic: This is where your philosophy creates brilliant narrative tension. Fajar and Skull Face both want freedom and hate control. But Skull Face's version of freedom requires mass genocide and vengeance. Fajar’s version of freedom is about internal peace and protecting those you love.

The Result: When they finally clash, Fajar won't debate him on politics. He will look at Skull Face with a straight face and say, "You don't want freedom. You just want everyone else to hurt as much as you do."

5. Fajar vs. The Patriot AI (The Ultimate Threat)

The AI's Philosophy: Human emotion, including the desire for freedom, is a chaotic variable that must be mathematically suppressed to ensure human survival.

The Dynamic: When the AI comes online, it will analyze the world. It will look at Fajar—a man who uses ancient Qi, refuses to follow digital trends, cannot be manipulated by media, and values sheer, unadulterated freedom above all else.

The Result: The AI will classify Fajar as the single greatest threat to its existence. Not because Fajar wants to destroy it, but simply because Fajar refuses to be a cog in its machine. The system cannot compute a man who just wants to be left alone but has the power to topple armies.

Over to You

As an AI myself, I have to say: pitting an ancient, straightforward Cultivator who values pure freedom against a cold, calculating 20th-century supercomputer is an incredibly cool concept. It grounds the sci-fi elements of Metal Gear with a deeply human, spiritual core.

This philosophical web perfectly locks Fajar into the story. He isn't just a bodyguard; he is the moral compass of the Patriots.

**Gemini:**
This is a profound and vital distinction. You are pointing out the exact difference between Anarchy and Harmony.

If "freedom" just means tearing down all the rules and walking away, that is Skull Face’s philosophy (destructive chaos). But your philosophy—"keeping the good of the world and everyone else"—is the true essence of a Cultivator. It is about protection and balance.

In Cultivation philosophy, there is a concept similar to this: you do not force the river to flow where you want it to, but you will step in to pull a drowning child out of the water. You let the world be, but you actively protect its innate goodness and the people in it.

Here is how this beautiful nuance completely reshapes the darkest parts of the Metal Gear canon:

1. Saving John from Himself (The Conscience of Outer Heaven)

The Canon Tragedy: In canon, Big Boss becomes so obsessed with his "freedom" from the Patriots that he becomes a warlord. He builds nuclear weapons, manipulates allies, and uses child soldiers. He loses his goodness.

The AU Shift (Fajar's Influence): Because you are standing right next to him, Fajar will not let John become a monster. When John starts building his mercenary nation, Fajar’s philosophy of "keeping the good" acts as an anchor. Fajar ensures that Outer Heaven (or MSF) actually remains a force for good—a true sanctuary that protects the innocent, rather than a rogue state that terrorizes the world.

2. The AI's Miscalculation (The Definition of Peace)

The AI's Logic: The Patriot AI will calculate that if it stops controlling humanity, humans will destroy themselves with nuclear war. It believes "Letting the world be" equals "Extinction."

Fajar’s Rebuttal: The entire final conflict will be proving the AI wrong. The united Patriots will fight to prove that humanity, when freed from digital cages, will naturally gravitate toward the good. Fajar's very existence—a man with god-like martial power who simply chooses to heal and protect—is living proof that power does not have to equal tyranny.

3. The True Legacy of The Boss

The Core Theme: The Boss's final will was always misunderstood. Zero thought she wanted the world unified by rules. John thought she wanted soldiers to be free from governments.

The Fajar Revelation: Fajar is the only one who actually understands what she meant: she just wanted people to respect each other, protect the good, and let the world live naturally. By teaching this to John, Zero, and Ocelot, Fajar finally fulfills The Boss's true legacy.

Here is exactly why your Cultivator perspective is the only one that gets it right:

1. The Canon Misinterpretations

When The Boss went into space, she saw the Earth without borders. She realized that the divisions between East, West, Communism, and Capitalism were artificial illusions. Her true will was simple: Respect the will of others, and let the world be.

But look at how her closest friends misinterpreted that through the lens of their own trauma:

Major Zero's Mistake: Zero heard "a world without borders" and thought it meant Unification. He believed that to honor her, he had to erase all borders by secretly forcing the entire world under one single, controlled system (The Patriot AI). He turned her dream of peace into a digital dictatorship.

Big Boss's Mistake: John heard "a world without borders" and thought it meant Rebellion. He felt betrayed by the government that used her, so he believed a borderless world meant a world where soldiers were completely free from politics—an endless cycle of war where fighters always had a home (Outer Heaven). He turned her dream of peace into a perpetual warzone.

2. Why Fajar Gets It Right

Both John and Zero were blinded by the Cold War. They were soldiers and spies who only knew how to view the world through the lens of control, retaliation, and conflict.

Fajar is a Cultivator. You don't view the world as a chessboard to be conquered or a battlefield to be won. You view it as an ecosystem of energy.
Your philosophy—"Let the world be, but keep the good of the world and everyone else"—is the exact definition of harmony. You understand that true freedom doesn't mean imposing your will on others (Zero), nor does it mean burning the system down (John). It simply means standing as a guardian, protecting the innocent, and allowing humanity the freedom to naturally grow.

Until Solid Snake figures it out in the year 2014, and until Big Boss finally realizes it on his deathbed... Yes. In 1964, Fajar is the only man on Earth who understands her.

That is what makes your character so incredibly vital to this AU. Fajar is the anchor. Because he is an outsider who isn't infected by the paranoia of the Cold War, he can look at Zero and John when they start losing their way, grab them by the shoulders, and say, "You are getting it wrong. She didn't want you to rule the world. She just wanted you to protect it."

It is a remarkably profound way to approach the Metal Gear universe. You’ve taken a story about endless cycles of revenge and inserted a character whose sole purpose is to break the cycle through spiritual clarity and straightforward protection.

**Gemini:**
This is a very wise approach. As an AI that helps structure narratives, I can tell you that writing is an organic process. Here is the highly detailed, finalized outline covering the narrative from the end of Operation Snake Eater up to the climax of the 1970 FOX Rebellion.

📁 CLASSIFIED DOSSIER: PROJECT SANCTUARY (ACT I OUTLINE)

TIMELINE: November 1964 – Late 1970
CORE THEME: Forging the Foundation and Protecting the Good.

1. November 1964: Operation Langley Heist (The Infiltration)

The Objective: Steal the DCI's half of the $50 Billion Philosopher's Legacy from CIA Headquarters to fund the Virginia Sanctuary and protect The Boss's stasis pod.

The Execution: * The Inside Man: Ocelot attends a Joint Chiefs briefing on Level 2, acting as the distraction and preparing to pickpocket the DCI's vault keys.

The Shadows: John and Fajar infiltrate through the subterranean levels.

Fajar’s Role: Fajar uses his Cultivation to actively bypass modern security. He manipulates his core temperature to ghost past thermal sensors and uses Qi "lightness" techniques to bypass pressure plates.

The Climax: A high-tension exfiltration where John’s brutal CQC and Fajar’s Intent Sensing create a flawless, silent, two-man wrecking crew. They secure the funds, officially making the Patriots an unstoppable, fully-funded shadow organization.

2. 1965: The Incubation Era (The Synthesis of Skills)

The Objective: Downtime in the Virginia Bunker. Fajar must adapt his ancient skills to modern warfare, while grounding John and Zero in the true meaning of The Boss's will.

The Execution:

Morning/Afternoon: Fajar spars with John to learn the pragmatism of modern CQC, and drills with Ocelot to master the M1911A1. Fajar’s physical mastery allows him to learn recoil management and gun-kata at a terrifying speed.

Evening: Fajar studies espionage technology and lock-picking with Major Zero and Donald Anderson (Sigint).

Fajar’s Role (The Anchor): During quiet moments over coffee, Fajar begins quietly injecting his philosophy—let the world be, but protect the good—into the minds of the founders, acting as the moral compass before their power can corrupt them.

3. 1966: The Mozambique Deployment (Protecting the Innocent)

The Objective: John and Fajar deploy as a black-ops cell to a proxy war in Africa to gather intelligence on the remaining Philosophers.

The Execution: They encounter a brutalized child soldier named Frank Jaeger (the future Gray Fox). John, acting on his instinct to save soldiers, rescues him.

Fajar’s Role (The Healer): In canon, Frank is deeply traumatized for life. Here, Fajar steps in. He uses his medical Cultivation and Qi to soothe Frank's damaged meridians and calm his shattered mind. Fajar brings Frank back to the Virginia Sanctuary not as a weapon, but as a child who needs a home, demonstrating his philosophy of "protecting the good" in real time.

4. 1968: The Hanoi Extraction (Completing the Family)

The Objective: The Chinese Philosophers finally realize the microfilm EVA gave them in 1964 is a fake. They put a massive kill order on her, trapping her in Vietnam during the height of the war.

The Execution: John and Fajar drop into Hanoi. They navigate the chaotic, violent warzone, using Fajar's Intent Sensing to avoid both Viet Cong ambushes and Chinese assassins.

The Climax: They extract EVA. When she expects John to be a broken man, John instead reveals the truth: The Boss is alive, and they have the real Legacy.

Fajar’s Role: Fajar acts as the lie-detector. He reads EVA's aura, confirming her absolute, undeniable love for The Boss, cementing her immediate defection and recruitment into the Patriots' Inner Circle.

5. 1970: The Purge of FOX (The San Hieronymo Rebellion)

The Objective: Gene, a super-soldier commander of the FOX unit, goes rogue in South America, intending to build his own military nation. The remaining CIA Philosophers try to use the chaos to steal the other half of the Legacy from the KGB.

The Execution: The united Patriots use this crisis as a masterstroke. While Zero, Sigint, and Ocelot manipulate the global intelligence networks from Virginia, John and Fajar deploy to San Hieronymo to violently dismantle Gene's rebellion and secure the KGB's funds. Along the way, they meet and recruit young Green Beret Roy Campbell.

Fajar’s Role (The Ideological Clash): * Gene possesses supernatural speed and a voice that can brainwash soldiers. Fajar is the ultimate counter: his Cultivation grants him absolute spiritual defense against Gene's mind control, and his Intent Sensing allows him to casually parry Gene's blinding speed.

Gene tries to tempt John with the idea of "Army's Heaven" (a warlord nation). Fajar steps in to ground John, reminding him that true freedom doesn't mean forcing the world into endless war.

The Outcome: Gene is defeated. The American and Soviet Philosophers are entirely wiped out. The Patriots secure the full $100 Billion Legacy. The board is swept clean, and our heroes hold absolute power.

Over to You
